<user>117075172558147338198<//user><GmapID>0x80dcaef252b26209:0x69c371dd79e73b21</GmapID><Time>1615688374015<//Time><review>Super pretty trail with a nice view both up and down. It's an out and back so you can make it as short as you want. There are a lot of spots to stop and rest along the way and just take in the beautiful view.

It's a pretty easy hike. There's a steady incline on the way up and going down is quick and easy.

There's a free parking lot right at the head of the trail and some street parking if the lot is full. I came on a Saturday afternoon and there were still several spots when I arrived and the lot was almost empty when I left.<//review></record></dataset><record>

<Text>With so many great options for ramen in LA, it can be hard to find a spot that brings it. Iki ramen kills it. The LATimes review via Eater LA brought me and a friend here.

They recommended the burnt garlic bowl, and so would I. Although the broth is what I went for, the perfectly al dente noodles would bring me back. We were also a big fan of the pork bun. I dare to say that it was even better than the ramen. We also tried the crispy rice tuna appetizer. It was so close to being perfect. I loved the fresh tuna and the marinade, but the rice was ever so slightly too crispy.

The decor was minimalistic and cozy. The room itself was small, just like most ramen joints. It can be a little loud if every table is filled, but not unbearable.

Overall, I enjoyed my meal here and I would definitely come back if I were craving ramen in KTown.</Text><date>1550549662370</date>< name>

<UserId.>117872276526090591694</UserId.>< username>
Nicholas Dobkin</username>
<Date>1583731474475</Date>< Rate>
5< /Rate>
< Review>
Common wisdom has always held that however good Koreatown ramen was, it would always be second to the more iconic ramens of Little Tokyo and Sawtelle. With the recent arrival of a branch of Silverlake Ramen seeming to take top spot, it seemed like Ktown would forever live in the shadow of better ramen. Iki strikes out at that misconception with vigor, proving that breadth and depth of flavor can go hand in hand and in so doing, easily becoming one of the top ramen shops in Los Angeles.

Most ramen shops focus on doing one thing really well, whether it's the typical rich tonkotsu that anyone would like, or a specific niche that you can't get elsewhere. Iki kicks this cliche to the curb by creating a menu tailored to almost every taste in ramens, while never sacrificing the quality of the dishes.

For those seeking a rich pork broth, you'll want to go for the Burnt Garlic Tonkotsu. The smell alone outs it as the real deal, a tremendous broth full of savor. The eggs are perfectly cooked to occupy the glass-like medium texture between hard and melted yokes, making for a flavorful soft treasure of an egg. The pork is incredible, balancing crispy outsides juicy soft insides. The noodles are thin and hard, which isn't to my taste, but some will enjoy it and it certainly can't come close to ruining the dish. All alone this would be a worthy ramen for some. But it doesn't stop here.

For those seeking a lighter broth, iki has a refreshingly zesty yuzu shoyu. As a tonkotsu person myself I actually found the yuzu broth a bit of an acquired taste, but I know there will be people who love it. The interesting thing is that the noodle type for this bowl was different - a chewier wider noodle I enjoyed more.

It keeps going. Iki has vegan options in the form of its miso ramen and tan tan mazemen (soupless) which use impossible meat. I went with a vegan friend who said she enjoyed it although she noted that for those who want food which doesn't resemble meat, the dish is meant to resemble real pork visually, though she said she could distinguish the taste. Even so she liked the dish overall.

And just when you think you're done, Iki hits an absolute home run with it's desserts. Fans of black sesame will adore their creamy black sesame creme brulee, oozing with sesame flavor under it's freshly carmelized top layer. But my absolute favorite, possibly one of the best desserts I've ever had, was their yuzu ice cream. Smooth and citrusy, the cream is balanced by a sprinkle of brown palm sugar which adds a light crunch and incredible burst of flavor. It is truly an experience not to be missed for anyone looking for a great ice cream.

I haven't even dug through half the menu and when I think of their chicken paitan, special winter truffle butter and assortment of others, I can't avoid thinking of Iki as the menu that keeps giving. Parking is manageable and close, and lines are practically non-existant despite the shop being relatively small. The only reason K can see for this is that somehow no one knows Iki is here so if that describes you, here's the takeaway: Iki is the rising star of ramen in KTown - no matter what taste you bring to their table, you're sure to find something to love!< /Review>

<UserId.>104825526704332968516<//UserId.><username>Yoojin Smeeth<//username><Date>1571311864920< /Date>< rating>
4< /rating>
< Review>
New hip place in ktown for some ramen with great classics and twists from your usual tonkotsu. I love salmon, heard their quality is quite good, so I had to try some!

SALMON
Salmon Burrata  -- I had high hopes from reading reviews about this but thought it was so-so. Salmon wasn't incredible but burrata was rich and creamy. I thought there could be less yuzu flavor so the honey truffle could really shine.

Salmon ikura bowl -- I had this one for delivery on a separate day. I thought the salmon quality was so so again. But the rice was good and portion size was good. More salmon than the burrata dish, even at the same price, though this bowl was super simple and exactly was as the name says.

We tried each others' food cause friends, and general consensus :
RAMEN
- Tori paitan broth tastes like ham?
- Garlic tonkotsu has strong garlic flavor. Still good with depth in the flavor.
-Yuzu Shio was a favorite. Broth is flavorful and the yuzu cuts the richness of the ramen. Yuzu adds a slight fresh taste to ramen.

DESSERT
- Shio Koji Ice Cream - What is that? Get it.
Rich milky ice cream with tones of caramel. It was unique but familiar at the same time. Shio Koji is fermented rice (hey probiotics, it's like froyo now) but really don't let the fermented funk deter you from getting this. It's not sour at all. Especially if salted caramel ice cream is your flava!
-Yuzu ice cream - very lemony, this was too citrusy for me but friend really liked it.
-Black sesame creme brulee - classic with a twist! Popular in our group. Though Shio Koji was my fav!

I guess one thing that could be improved is phone communication?
Ok they really do not pick up their phone. Our group was kinda big (6 ppl) so I called a few times to ask if they took reservations -- after several days trying,  someone finally picked up, said "no" very bluntly and hung up. It felt like recieving a "kk" but in a call. Ok... Thanks...! Just wanted to ask.

But in person it was better. I came early to grab our party a table, luckily they put some tables together and easily we were all seated! Our server was kind and attentive throughout. :) It's not a big place and the place definitely got busy especially after 7 on sunday evening. They have a parking lot but shared amongst other businesses, it was definitely limited.</Review>

109118770207372986091< /user_id>
<username>John Dho<//username><Time>1552369727248</Time><Rate>5</Rate>< review>
Professional level repertory theater offering 7 or more shows a year at their home theater in East Sonora or at the historic Fallon House Theater in Columbia, a California State Historic Park. Artists come from around the country, lending a level of performance and professionalism not often seen in a small town theater. It's amazing that a small theater can continuously produce so many high quality shows year after year (this year, 2019, is their 40th anniversary year!) - but they do!

Both theaters are small - there's not a bad seat in the Sonora house but sight lines at the Fallon House can be tough for the vertically challenged!</review>

<Rate>5<//Rate><review>We saw State Fair yesterday and man, it was wonderful! We are huge fans of old musical theater, especially Rogers and Hammerstein. SRT NAILED State Fair. We are in absolute awe at how the tiny stage at the Fallon House was transformed into six different scenes to accommodate the story line. The house sounded fantastic - someone has engineered a great blend on the mics (the chorus parts were particularly robust). And then there is the cast...everyone did great, but just a few individuals made the show for me. Gary Martinez IS Abel Frake - such a spot on casting decision. Jerry Lee is a real pro. Such a great voice! I'd love to see him play Judd Frye in Oklahoma. My favorite of the entire production was Taylor Simmons...watch this kid! He's going to go very far. He's got great stage presence, a wonderful voice and this kid can DANCE! Watching him made me think I was seeing a young Astaire. I'd love to see him play Marius in Les Miserables. Don't assume that Sierra Rep is your average homegrown production. This is a quality company doing great stuff!</review>< pics>

<Rating>5</Rating>< Text>
Absolutely loved our first visit! Everything down to the minute details is very well thought out and carefully tailored for the Which Wich experience. I'll admit, I was hesitant at first, when my husband begged to go here, as I assumed it would be like a revamped subway. I was so wrong! We passed by the most wonderful lady (possible manager) on the way to the establishment, and let our kids see the pavilion fountain that is set up in the middle of the walking area. Once we arrived at Which Wich, the same lady came out to us in line and handed our boys two huge stickers and two pennies for the boys to throw into the fountain. Just knowing she made note that they loved the fountain when she walked by, went into her work and gave them coins to enjoy the water with really made their day. The food was awesome- both my kids devoured their ice cream cookie, and my husband and I ate every single bite of our sandwiches (I had a turkey club, and my husband had a meatball sandwich). Towards the end of our visit, the same wonderful employee came back out to us to check on us and see how we were doing. Overall, we will be back, as it was an amazing experience. Restaurants rarely have this kind of customer professionalism and care!< /Text>

<name>Pranav Deshpande</name><Time>1612662529470< /Time><Rate>5</Rate>< text>
Huddart Park is a beautiful park for hike around multiple trails. It is thickly wooded and the trails are well marked.

One can choose trails which are flat or have moderate elevation. There is open space where one can play simple games. There is a sand volley ball court too. And a badminton court. Lots of picnic areas around.

Ample parking across multiple parking lots. Entry fee is $6 per car. Make sure that you carry exact cash if possible, as if the booth is not manned you'll have to drop the fee in a box.

Overall, a fantastic place to spend time with friends and family.<//text>

<rate>5<//rate><text>Lonely Trail to Richards Road loop trail is part of Huddart park. Park hours are till 5 pm so parking outside would be a good option, in case you can not get back by 5pm. Park has a big parking lot. Restrooms are available at the trailhead. It‚Äôs around an 8.5 mile moderate hike. We completed it in 4hrs. Trail is shaded, lots of Redwood trees. Keep the trail map handy all the time as there are many diversions, and easy to get off track. There are logs and fallen trees across the trail, be careful while crossing them. Overall nice, quiet hike, good workout. One on the trail, it‚Äôs pretty straight forward. No hidden paths or uncertainties. The markers are short and hard to find from the lot so be sure to ask the ranger about where to start.

Nice quiet park. $6 entrance fee per vehicle, but worth it since there's about parking and no worries of looking for a spot. There are several picnic area which can be reserved online, and some drop in picnic areas. Also had 2 sand volleyball courts. Ranger recommended a 5 mile loop (Crystal spring to Dean trail), which is largely shared and passes through lush redwood groves. There's also a shorter 3 mile loop and a liner 10 mile loop that the ranger recommended. Be sure to grab a map as the week meaning sign pays can be quite confusing.<//Review>
